branches of live oak, loving lounger in my\r\n      winding paths, it shall be you!\r\n  Hands I have taken, face I have kiss\xe2\x80\x99d, mortal I have ever touch\xe2\x80\x99d,\r\n      it shall be you.\r\n\r\n  I dote on myself, there is that lot of me and all so luscious,\r\n  Each moment and whatever happens thrills me with joy,\r\n  I cannot tell how my ankles bend, nor whence the cause of my faintest wish,\r\n  Nor the cause of the friendship I emit, nor the cause of the\r\n      friendship I take again.\r\n\r\n  That I walk up my stoop, I pause to consider if it really be,\r\n  A morning-glory at my window satisfies me more than the metaphysics\r\n      of books.\r\n\r\n  To behold the day-break!\r\n  The little light fades the immense and diaphanous shadows,\r\n  The air tastes good to my palate.\r\n\r\n  Hefts of the moving world at innocent gambols silently rising\r\n      freshly exuding,\r\n  Scooting obliquely high and low.\r\n\r\n  Something I cannot see puts upward libidinous prongs,\r\n  Seas of bright juice suffuse heaven.\r\n\r\n  The earth by the sky staid with, the daily close of their junction,\r\n  The heav\xe2\x80\x99d challenge from the east that moment over my head,\r\n  The mocking taunt, See then whether you shall be master!\r\n\r\n       25\r\n  Dazzling and tremendous how quick the sun-rise would kill me,\r\n  If I could not now and always send sun-rise out of me.\r\n\r\n  We also ascend dazzling and tremendous as the sun,\r\n  We found our own O my soul in the calm and cool of the daybreak.\r\n\r\n  My voice goes after what my eyes cannot reach,\r\n  With the twirl of my tongue I encompass worlds and volumes of worlds.\r\n\r\n  Speech is the twin of my vision, it is unequal to measure itself,\r\n  It provokes me forever, it says sarcastically,\r\n  Walt you contain enough, why don\xe2\x80\x99t you let it out then?\r\n\r\n  Come now I will not be tantalized, you conceive too much of\r\n      articulation,\r\n  Do you not know O speech how the buds beneath you are folded?\r\n  Waiting in gloom, protected by frost,\r\n  The dirt receding before my prophetical screams,\r\n  I underlying causes to balance them at last,\r\n  My knowledge my live parts, it keeping tally with the meaning of all things,\r\n  Happiness, (which whoever hears me let him or her set out in search\r\n      of this day.)\r\n\r\n  My final merit I refuse you, I refuse putting from me what I really am,\r\n  Encompass worlds, but never try to encompass me,\r\n  I crowd your sleekest and best by simply looking toward you.\r\n\r\n  Writing and talk do not prove me,\r\n  I carry the plenum of proof and every thing else in my face,\r\n  With the hush of my lips I wholly confound the skeptic.\r\n\r\n       26\r\n  Now I will do nothing but listen,\r\n  To accrue what I hear into this song, to let sounds contribute toward it.\r\n\r\n  I hear bravuras of birds, bustle of growing wheat, gossip of flames,\r\n      clack of sticks cooking my meals,\r\n  I hear the sound I love, the sound of the human voice,\r\n  I hear all sounds running together, combined, fused or following,\r\n  Sounds of the city and sounds out of the city, sounds of the day and night,\r\n  Talkative young ones to those that like them, the loud laugh of\r\n      work-people at their meals,\r\n  The angry base of disjointed friendship, the faint tones of the sick,\r\n  The judge with hands tight to the desk, his pallid lips pronouncing\r\n      a death-sentence,\r\n  The heave\xe2\x80\x99e\xe2\x80\x99yo of stevedores unlading ships by the wharves, the\r\n      refrain of the anchor-lifters,\r\n  The ring of alarm-bells, the cry of fire, the whirr of swift-streaking\r\n      engines and hose-carts with premonitory tinkles and color\xe2\x80\x99d lights,\r\n  The steam-whistle, the solid roll of the train of approaching cars,\r\n  The slow march play\xe2\x80\x99d at the head of the association marching two and two,\r\n  (They go to guard some corpse, the flag-tops are draped with black muslin.)\r\n\r\n  I hear the violoncello, (\xe2\x80\x99tis the young man\xe2\x80\x99s heart\xe2\x80\x99s complaint,)\r\n  I hear the key\xe2\x80\x99d cornet, it glides quickly in through my ears,\r\n  It shakes mad-sweet pangs through my belly and breast.\r\n\r\n  I hear the chorus, it is a grand opera,\r\n  Ah this indeed is music--this suits me.\r\n\r\n  A tenor large and fresh as the creation fills me,\r\n  The orbic flex of his mouth is pouring and filling me full.\r\n\r\n  I hear the train\xe2\x80\x99d soprano (what work with hers is this?)\r\n  The orchestra whirls me wider than Uranus flies,\r\n  It wrenches such ardors from me I did not know I possess\xe2\x80\x99d them,\r\n  It sails me, I dab with bare feet, they are lick\xe2\x80\x99d by the indolent waves,\r\n  I am cut by bitter and angry hail, I lose my breath,\r\n  Steep\xe2\x80\x99d amid honey\xe2\x80\x99d morphine, my windpipe throttled in fakes of death,\r\n  At length let up again to feel the puzzle of puzzles,\r\n  And that we call Being.\r\n\r\n       27\r\n  To be in any form, what is that?\r\n  (Round and round we go, all of us, and ever come back thither,)\r\n  If nothing lay more develop\xe2\x80\x99d the quahaug in its callous shell were enough.\r\n\r\n  Mine is no callous shell,\r\n  I have instant conductors all over me whether I pass or stop,\r\n  They seize every object and lead it harmlessly through me.\r\n\r\n  I merely stir, press, feel with my fingers, and am happy,\r\n  To touch my person to some one else\xe2\x80\x99s is about as much as I can stand.\r\n\r\n       28\r\n  Is this then a touch? quivering me to a new identity,\r\n  Flames and ether making a rush for my veins,\r\n  Treacherous tip of me reaching and crowding to help them,\r\n  My flesh and blood playing out lightning to strike what is hardly\r\n      different from myself,\r\n  On all sides prurient provokers stiffening my limbs,\r\n  Straining the udder of my heart for its withheld drip,\r\n  Behaving licentious toward me, taking no denial,\r\n  Depriving me of my best as for a purpose,\r\n  Unbuttoning my clothes, holding me by the bare waist,\r\n  Deluding my confusion with the calm of the sunlight and pasture-fields,\r\n  Immodestly sliding the fellow-senses away,\r\n  They bribed to swap off with touch and go and graze at the edges of me,\r\n  No consideration, no regard for my draining strength or my anger,\r\n  Fetching the rest of the herd around to enjoy them a while,\r\n  Then all uniting to stand on a headland and worry me.\r\n\r\n  The sentries desert every other part of me,\r\n  They have left me helpless to a red marauder,\r\n  They all come to the headland to witness and assist against me.\r\n\r\n  I am given up by traitors,\r\n  I talk wildly, I have lost my wits, I and nobody else am the\r\n      greatest traitor,\r\n  I went myself first to the headland, my own hands carried me there.\r\n\r\n  You villain touch! what are you doing? my breath is tight in its throat,\r\n  Unclench your floodgates, you are too much for me.\r\n\r\n       29\r\n  Blind loving wrestling touch, sheath\xe2\x80\x99d hooded sharp-tooth\xe2\x80\x99d touch!\r\n  Did it make you ache so, leaving me?\r\n\r\n  Parting track\xe2\x80\x99d by arriving, perpetual payment of perpetual loan,\r\n  Rich showering rain, and recompense richer afterward.\r\n\r\n  Sprouts take and accumulate, stand by the curb prolific and vital,\r\n  Landscapes projected masculine, full-sized and golden.\r\n\r\n       30\r\n  All truths wait in all things,\r\n  They neither hasten their own delivery nor resist it,\r\n  They do not need the obstetric forceps of the surgeon,\r\n  The insignificant is as big to me as any,\r\n  (What is less or more than a touch?)\r\n\r\n  Logic and sermons never convince,\r\n  The damp of the night drives deeper into my soul.\r\n\r\n  (Only what proves itself to every man and woman is so,\r\n  Only what nobody denies is so.)\r\n\r\n  A minute and a drop of me settle my brain,\r\n  I believe the soggy clods shall become lovers and lamps,\r\n  And a compend of compends is the meat of a man or woman,\r\n  And a summit and flower there is the feeling they have for each other,\r\n  And they are to branch boundlessly out of that lesson until it\r\n      becomes omnific,\r\n  And until one and all shall delight us, and we them.\r\n\r\n       31\r\n  I believe a leaf of grass is no less than the journey work of the stars,\r\n  And the pismire is equally perfect, and a grain of sand, and the egg\r\n      of the wren,\r\n  And the tree-toad is a chef-d\xe2\x80\x99\xc5\x93uvre for the highest,\r\n  And the running blackberry would adorn the parlors of heaven,\r\n  And the narrowest hinge in my hand puts to scorn all machinery,\r\n  And the cow crunching with depress\xe2\x80\x99d head surpasses any statue,\r\n  And a mouse is miracle enough to stagger sextillions of infidels.\r\n\r\n  I find I incorporate gneiss, coal, long-threaded moss, fruits,\r\n      grains, esculent roots,\r\n  And am stucco\xe2\x80\x99d with quadrupeds and birds all over,\r\n  And have distanced what is behind me for good reasons,\r\n  But call any thing back again when I desire it.\r\n\r\n  In vain the speeding or shyness,\r\n  In vain the plutonic rocks send their old heat against my approach,\r\n  In vain the mastodon retreats beneath its own powder\xe2\x80\x99d bones,\r\n  In vain objects stand leagues off and assume manifold shapes,\r\n  In vain the ocean settling in hollows and the great monsters lying low,\r\n  In vain the buzzard houses herself with the sky,\r\n  In vain the snake slides through the creepers and logs,\r\n  In vain the elk takes to the inner passes of the woods,\r\n  In vain the razor-bill\xe2\x80\x99d auk sails far north to Labrador,\r\n  I follow quickly, I ascend to the nest in the fissure of the cliff.\r\n\r\n       32\r\n  I think I could turn and live with animals, they are so placid and\r\n      self-contain\xe2\x80\x99d,\r\n  I stand and look at them long and long.\r\n\r\n  They do not sweat and whine about their condition,\r\n  They do not lie awake in the dark and weep for their sins,\r\n  They do not make me sick discussing their duty to God,\r\n  Not one is dissatisfied, not one is demented with the mania of\r\n      owning things,\r\n  Not one kneels to another, nor to his kind that lived thousands of\r\n      years ago,\r\n  Not one is respectable or unhappy over the whole earth.\r\n\r\n  So they show their relations to me and I accept them,\r\n  They bring me tokens of myself, they evince them plainly in their\r\n      possession.\r\n\r\n  I wonder where they get those tokens,\r\n  Did I pass that way huge times ago and negligently drop them?\r\n\r\n  Myself moving forward then and now and forever,\r\n  Gathering and showing more always and with velocity,\r\n  Infinite and omnigenous, and the like of these among them,\r\n  Not too exclusive toward the reachers of my remembrancers,\r\n  Picking out here one that I love, and now go with him on brotherly terms.\r\n\r\n  A gigantic beauty of a stallion, fresh and responsive to my caresses,\r\n  Head high in the forehead, wide between the ears,\r\n  Limbs glossy and supple, tail dusting the ground,\r\n  Eyes full of sparkling wickedness, ears finely cut, flexibly moving.\r\n\r\n  His nostrils dilate as my heels embrace him,\r\n  His well-built limbs tremble with pleasure as we race around and return.\r\n\r\n  I but use you a minute, then I resign you, stallion,\r\n  Why do I need your paces when I myself out-gallop them?\r\n  Even as I stand or sit passing faster than you.\r\n\r\n       33\r\n  Space and Time! now I see it is true, what I guess\xe2\x80\x99d at,\r\n  What I guess\xe2\x80\x99d when I loaf\xe2\x80\x99d on the grass,\r\n  What I guess\xe2\x80\x99d while I lay alone in my bed,\r\n  And again as I walk\xe2\x80\x99d the beach under the paling stars of the morning.\r\n\r\n  My ties and ballasts leave me, my elbows rest in sea-gaps,\r\n  I skirt sierras, my palms cover continents,\r\n  I am afoot with my vision.\r\n\r\n  By the city\xe2\x80\x99s quadrangular houses--in log huts, camping with lumber-men,\r\n  Along the ruts of the turnpike, along the dry gulch and rivulet bed,\r\n  Weeding my onion-patch or hosing rows of carrots and parsnips,\r\n      crossing savannas, trailing in forests,\r\n  Prospecting, gold-digging, girdling the trees of a new purchase,\r\n  Scorch\xe2\x80\x99d ankle-deep by the hot sand, hauling my boat down the\r\n      shallow river,\r\n  Where the panther walks to and fro on a limb overhead, where the\r\n      buck turns furiously at the hunter,\r\n  Where the rattlesnake suns his flabby length on a rock, where the\r\n      otter is feeding on fish,\r\n  Where the alligator in his tough pimples sleeps by the bayou,\r\n  Where the black bear is searching for roots or honey, where the\r\n      beaver pats the mud with his paddle-shaped tall;\r\n  Over the growing sugar, over the yellow-flower\xe2\x80\x99d cotton plant, over\r\n      the rice in its low moist field,\r\n  Over the sharp-peak\xe2\x80\x99d farm house, with its scallop\xe2\x80\x99d scum and\r\n      slender shoots from the gutters,\r\n  Over the western persimmon, over the long-leav\xe2\x80\x99d corn, over the\r\n      delicate blue-flower flax,\r\n  Over the white and brown buckwheat, a hummer and buzzer there with\r\n      the rest,\r\n  Over the dusky green of the rye as it ripples and shades in the breeze;\r\n  Scaling mountains, pulling myself cautiously up, holding on by low\r\n      scragged limbs,\r\n  Walking the path worn in the grass and beat through the leaves of the brush,\r\n  Where the quail is whistling betwixt the woods and the wheat-lot,\r\n  Where the bat flies in the Seventh-month eve, where the great\r\n      goldbug drops through the dark,\r\n  Where the brook puts out of the roots of the old tree and flows to\r\n      the meadow,\r\n  Where cattle stand and shake away flies with the tremulous\r\n      shuddering of their hides,\r\n  Where the cheese-cloth hangs in the kitchen, where andirons straddle\r\n      the hearth-slab, where cobwebs fall in festoons from the rafters;\r\n  Where trip-hammers crash, where the press is whirling its cylinders,\r\n  Wherever the human heart beats with terrible throes under its ribs,\r\n  Where the pear-shaped balloon is floating aloft, (floating in it\r\n      myself and looking composedly down,)\r\n  Where the life-car is drawn on the slip-noose, where the heat\r\n      hatches pale-green eggs in the dented sand,\r\n  Where the she-whale swims with her calf and never forsakes it,\r\n  Where the steam-ship trails hind-ways its long pennant of smoke,\r\n  Where the fin of the shark cuts like a black chip out of the water,\r\n  Where the half-burn\xe2\x80\x99d brig is riding on unknown currents,\r\n  Where shells grow to her slimy deck, where the dead are corrupting below;\r\n  Where the dense-starr\xe2\x80\x99d flag is borne at the head of the regiments,\r\n  Approaching Manhattan up by the long-stretching island,\r\n  Under Niagara, the cataract falling like a veil over my countenance,\r\n  Upon a door-step, upon the horse-block of hard wood outside,\r\n  Upon the race-course, or enjoying picnics or jigs or a good game of\r\n      base-ball,\r\n  At he-festivals, with blackguard gibes, ironical license,\r\n      bull-dances, drinking, laughter,\r\n  At the cider-mill tasting the sweets of the brown mash, sucking the\r\n      juice through a straw,\r\n  At apple-peelings wanting kisses for all the red fruit I find,\r\n  At musters, beach-parties, friendly bees, huskings, house-raisings;\r\n  Where the mocking-bird sounds his delicious gurgles, cackles,\r\n      screams, weeps,\r\n  Where the hay-rick stands in the barn-yard, where the dry-stalks are\r\n      scatter\xe2\x80\x99d, where the brood-cow waits in the hovel,\r\n  Where the bull advances to do his masculine work, where the stud to\r\n      the mare, where the cock is treading the hen,\r\n  Where the heifers browse, where geese nip their food with short jerks,\r\n  Where sun-down shadows lengthen over the limitless and lonesome prairie,\r\n  Where herds of buffalo make a crawling spread of the square miles\r\n      far and near,\r\n  Where the humming-bird shimmers, where the neck of the long-lived\r\n      swan is curving and winding,\r\n  Where the laughing-gull scoots by the shore, where she laughs her\r\n      near-human laugh,\r\n  Where bee-hives range on a gray bench in the garden half hid by the\r\n      high weeds,\r\n  Where band-neck\xe2\x80\x99d partridges roost in a ring on the ground with\r\n      their heads out,\r\n  Where burial coaches enter the arch\xe2\x80\x99d gates of a cemetery,\r\n  Where winter wolves bark amid wastes of snow and icicled trees,\r\n  Where the yellow-crown\xe2\x80\x99d heron comes to the edge of the marsh at\r\n      night and feeds upon small crabs,\r\n  Where the splash of swimmers and divers cools the warm noon,\r\n  Where the katy-did works her chromatic reed on the walnut-tree over\r\n      the well,\r\n  Through patches of citrons and cucumbers with silver-wired leaves,\r\n  Through the salt-lick or orange glade, or under conical firs,\r\n  Through the gymnasium, through the curtain\xe2\x80\x99d saloon, through the\r\n      office or public hall;\r\n  Pleas\xe2\x80\x99d with the native and pleas\xe2\x80\x99d with the foreign, pleas\xe2\x80\x99d with\r\n      the new and old,\r\n  Pleas\xe2\x80\x99d with the homely woman as well as the handsome,\r\n  Pleas\xe2\x80\x99d with the quakeress as she puts off her bonnet and talks melodiously,\r\n  Pleas\xe2\x80\x99d with the tune of the choir of the whitewash\xe2\x80\x99d church,\r\n  Pleas\xe2\x80\x99d with the earnest words of the sweating Methodist preacher,\r\n      impress\xe2\x80\x99d seriously at the camp-meeting;\r\n  Looking in at the shop-windows of Broadway the whole forenoon,\r\n      flatting the flesh of my nose on the thick plate glass,\r\n  Wandering the same afternoon with my face turn\xe2\x80\x99d up to the clouds,\r\n      or down a lane or along the beach,\r\n  My right and left arms round the sides of two friends, and I in the middle;\r\n  Coming home with the silent and dark-cheek\xe2\x80\x99d bush-boy, (behind me\r\n      he rides at the drape of the day,)\r\n  Far from the settlements studying the print of animals\xe2\x80\x99 feet, or the\r\n      moccasin print,\r\n  By the cot in the hospital reaching lemonade to a feverish patient,\r\n  Nigh the coffin\xe2\x80\x99d corpse when all is still, examining with a candle;\r\n  Voyaging to every port to dicker and adventure,\r\n  Hurrying with the modern crowd as eager and fickle as any,\r\n  Hot toward one I hate, ready in my madness to knife him,\r\n  Solitary at midnight in my back yard, my thoughts gone from me a long while,\r\n  Walking the old hills of Judaea with the beautiful gentle God by my side,\r\n  Speeding through space, speeding through heaven and the stars,\r\n  Speeding amid the seven satellites and the broad ring, and the\r\n      diameter of eighty thousand miles,\r\n  Speeding with tail\xe2\x80\x99d meteors, throwing fire-balls like the rest,\r\n  Carrying the crescent child that carries its own full mother in its belly,\r\n  Storming, enjoying, planning, loving, cautioning,\r\n  Backing and filling, appearing and disappearing,\r\n  I tread day and night such roads.\r\n\r\n  I visit the orchards of spheres and look at the product,\r\n  And look at quintillions ripen\xe2\x80\x99d and look at quintillions green.\r\n\r\n  I fly those flights of a fluid and swallowing soul,\r\n  My course runs below the soundings of plummets.\r\n\r\n  I help myself to material and immaterial,\r\n  No guard can shut me off, no law prevent me.\r\n\r\n  I anchor my ship for a little while only,\r\n  My messengers continually cruise away or bring their returns to me.\r\n\r\n  I go hunting polar furs and the seal, leaping chasms with a\r\n      pike-pointed staff, clinging to topples of brittle and blue.\r\n\r\n  I ascend to the foretruck,\r\n  I take my place late at night in the crow\xe2\x80\x99s-nest,\r\n  We sail the arctic sea, it is plenty light enough,\r\n  Through the clear atmosphere I stretch around on the wonderful beauty,\r\n  The enormous masses of ice pass me and I pass them, the scenery is\r\n      plain in all directions,\r\n  The white-topt mountains show in the distance, I fling out my\r\n      fancies toward them,\r\n  We are approaching some great battle-field in which we are soon to\r\n      be engaged,\r\n  We pass the colossal outposts of the encampment, we pass with still\r\n      feet and caution,\r\n  Or we are entering by the suburbs some vast and ruin\xe2\x80\x99d city,\r\n  The blocks and fallen architecture more than all the living cities\r\n      of the globe.\r\n\r\n  I am a free companion, I bivouac by invading watchfires,\r\n  I turn the bridegroom out of bed and stay with the bride myself,\r\n  I tighten her all night to my thighs and lips.\r\n\r\n  My voice is the wife\xe2\x80\x99s voice, the screech by the rail of the stairs,\r\n  They fetch my man\xe2\x80\x99s body up dripping and drown\xe2\x80\x99d.\r\n\r\n  I understand the large hearts of heroes,\r\n  The courage of present times and all times,\r\n  How the skipper saw the crowded and rudderless wreck of the\r\n      steamship, and Death chasing it up and down the storm,\r\n  How he knuckled tight and gave not back an inch, and was faithful of\r\n      days and faithful of nights,\r\n  And chalk\xe2\x80\x99d in large letters on a board, Be of good cheer, we will\r\n      not desert you;\r\n  How he follow\xe2\x80\x99d with them and tack\xe2\x80\x99d with them three days and\r\n      would not give it up,\r\n  How he saved the drifting company at last,\r\n  How the lank loose-gown\xe2\x80\x99d women look\xe2\x80\x99d when boated from the\r\n      side of their prepared graves,\r\n  How the silent old-faced infants and the lifted sick, and the\r\n      sharp-lipp\xe2\x80\x99d unshaved men;\r\n  All this I swallow, it tastes good, I like it well, it becomes mine,\r\n  I am the man, I suffer\xe2\x80\x99d, I was there.\r\n\r\n  The disdain and calmness of martyrs,\r\n  The mother of old, condemn\xe2\x80\x99d for a witch, burnt with dry wood, her\r\n      children gazing on,\r\n  The hounded slave that flags in the race, leans by the fence,\r\n      blowing, cover\xe2\x80\x99d with sweat,\r\n  The twinges that sting like needles his legs and neck, the murderous\r\n      buckshot and the bullets,\r\n  All these I feel or am.\r\n\r\n  I am the hounded slave, I wince at the bite of the dogs,\r\n  Hell and despair are upon me, crack and again crack the marksmen,\r\n  I clutch the rails of the fence, my gore dribs, thinn\xe2\x80\x99d with the\r\n      ooze of my skin,\r\n  I fall on the weeds and stones,\r\n  The riders spur their unwilling horses, haul close,\r\n  Taunt my dizzy ears and beat me violently over the head with whip-stocks.\r\n\r\n  Agonies are one of my changes of garments,\r\n  I do not ask the wounded person how he feels, I myself become the\r\n      wounded person,\r\n  My hurts turn livid upon me as I lean on a cane and observe.\r\n\r\n  I am the mash\xe2\x80\x99d fireman with breast-bone broken,\r\n  Tumbling walls buried me in their debris,\r\n  Heat and smoke I inspired, I heard the yelling shouts of my comrades,\r\n  I heard the distant click of their picks and shovels,\r\n  They have clear\xe2\x80\x99d the beams away, they tenderly lift me forth.\r\n\r\n  I lie in the night air in my red shirt, the pervading hush is for my sake,\r\n  Painless after all I lie exhausted but not so unhappy,\r\n  White and beautiful are the faces around me, the heads are bared\r\n      of their fire-caps,\r\n  The kneeling crowd fades with the light of the torches.\r\n\r\n  Distant and dead resuscitate,\r\n  They show as the dial or move as the hands of me, I am the clock myself.\r\n\r\n  I am an old artillerist, I tell of my fort\xe2\x80\x99s bombardment,\r\n  I am there again.\r\n\r\n  Again the long roll of the drummers,\r\n  Again the attacking cannon, mortars,\r\n  Again to my listening ears the cannon responsive.\r\n\r\n  I take part, I see and hear the whole,\r\n  The cries, curses, roar, the plaudits for well-aim\xe2\x80\x99d shots,\r\n  The ambulanza slowly passing trailing its red drip,\r\n  Workmen searching after damages, making indispensable repairs,\r\n  The fall of grenades through the rent roof, the fan-shaped explosion,\r\n  The whizz of limbs, heads, stone, wood, iron, high in the air.\r\n\r\n  Again gurgles the mouth of my dying general, he furiously waves\r\n      with his hand,\r\n  He gasps through the clot Mind not me--mind--the entrenchments.\r\n\r\n       34\r\n  Now I tell what I knew in Texas in my early youth,\r\n  (I tell not the fall of Alamo,\r\n  Not one escaped to tell the fall of Alamo,\r\n  The hundred and fifty are dumb yet at Alamo,)\r\n  \xe2\x80\x99Tis the tale of the murder in cold blood of four hundred and twelve\r\n      young men.\r\n\r\n  Retreating they had form\xe2\x80\x99d in a hollow square with their baggage for\r\n      breastworks,\r\n  Nine hundred lives out of the surrounding enemies, nine times their\r\n      number, was the price they took in advance,\r\n  Their colonel was wounded and their ammunition gone,\r\n  They treated for an honorable capitulation, receiv\xe2\x80\x99d writing and\r\n      seal, gave up their arms and march\xe2\x80\x99d back prisoners of war.\r\n\r\n  They were the glory of the race of rangers,\r\n  Matchless with horse, rifle, song, supper, courtship,\r\n  Large, turbulent, generous, handsome, proud, and affectionate,\r\n  Bearded, sunburnt, drest in the free costume of hunters,\r\n  Not a single one over thirty years of age.\r\n\r\n  The second First-day morning they were brought out in squads and\r\n      massacred, it was beautiful early summer,\r\n  The work commenced about five o\xe2\x80\x99clock and was over by eight.\r\n\r\n  None obey\xe2\x80\x99d the command to kneel,\r\n  Some made a mad and helpless rush, some stood stark and straight,\r\n  A few fell at once, shot in the temple or heart, the living and dead\r\n      lay together,\r\n  The maim\xe2\x80\x99d and mangled dug in the dirt, the new-comers saw them there,\r\n  Some half-kill\xe2\x80\x99d attempted to crawl away,\r\n  These were despatch\xe2\x80\x99d with bayonets or batter\xe2\x80\x99d with the blunts of muskets,\r\n  A youth not seventeen years old seiz\xe2\x80\x99d his assassin till two more\r\n      came to release him,\r\n  The three were all torn and cover\xe2\x80\x99d with the boy\xe2\x80\x99s blood.\r\n\r\n  At eleven o\xe2\x80\x99clock began the burning of the bodies;\r\n  That is the tale of the murder of the four hundred and twelve young men.\r\n\r\n       35\r\n  Would you hear of an old-time sea-fight?\r\n  Would you learn who won by the light of the moon and stars?\r\n  List to the yarn, as my grandmother\xe2\x80\x99s father the sailor told it to me.\r\n\r\n  Our foe was no skulk in his ship I tell you, (said he,)\r\n  His was the surly English pluck, and there is no tougher or truer,\r\n      and never was, and never will be;\r\n  Along the lower\xe2\x80\x99d eve he came horribly raking us.\r\n\r\n  We closed with him, the yards entangled, the cannon touch\xe2\x80\x99d,\r\n  My captain lash\xe2\x80\x99d fast with his own hands.\r\n\r\n  We had receiv\xe2\x80\x99d some eighteen pound shots under the water,\r\n  On our lower-gun-deck two large pieces had burst at the first fire,\r\n      killing all around and blowing up overhead.\r\n\r\n  Fighting at sun-down, fighting at dark,\r\n  Ten o\xe2\x80\x99clock at night, the full moon well up, our leaks on the gain,\r\n      and five feet of water reported,\r\n  The master-at-arms loosing the prisoners confined in the after-hold\r\n      to give them a chance for themselves.\r\n\r\n  The transit to and from the magazine is now stopt by the sentinels,\r\n  They see so many strange faces they do not know whom to trust.\r\n\r\n  Our frigate takes fire,\r\n  The other asks if we demand quarter?\r\n  If our colors are struck and the fighting done?\r\n\r\n  Now I laugh content, for I hear the voice of my little captain,\r\n  We have not struck, he composedly cries, we have just begun our part\r\n      of the fighting.\r\n\r\n  Only three guns are in use,\r\n  One is directed by the captain himself against the enemy\xe2\x80\x99s main-mast,\r\n  Two well serv\xe2\x80\x99d with grape and canister silence his musketry and\r\n      clear his decks.\r\n\r\n  The tops alone second the fire of this little battery, especially\r\n      the main-top,\r\n  They hold out bravely during the whole of the action.\r\n\r\n  Not a moment\xe2\x80\x99s cease,\r\n  The leaks gain fast on the pumps, the fire eats toward the powder-magazine.\r\n\r\n  One of the pumps has been shot away, it is generally thought we are sinking.\r\n\r\n  Serene stands the little captain,\r\n  He is not hurried, his voice is neither high nor low,\r\n  His eyes give more light to us than our battle-lanterns.\r\n\r\n  Toward twelve there in the beams of the moon they surrender to us.\r\n\r\n       36\r\n  Stretch\xe2\x80\x99d and still lies the midnight,\r\n  Two great hulls motionless on the breast of the darkness,\r\n  Our vessel riddled and slowly sinking, preparations to pass to the\r\n      one we have conquer\xe2\x80\x99d,\r\n  The captain on the quarter-deck coldly giving his orders through a\r\n      countenance white as a sheet,\r\n  Near by the corpse of the child that serv\xe2\x80\x99d in the cabin,\r\n  The dead face of an old salt with long white hair and carefully\r\n      curl\xe2\x80\x99d whiskers,\r\n  The flames spite of all that can be done flickering aloft and below,\r\n  The husky voices of the two or three officers yet fit for duty,\r\n  Formless stacks of bodies and bodies by themselves, dabs of flesh\r\n      upon the masts and spars,\r\n  Cut of cordage, dangle of rigging, slight shock of the soothe of waves,\r\n  Black and impassive guns, litter of powder-parcels, strong scent,\r\n  A few large stars overhead, silent and mournful shining,\r\n  Delicate sniffs of sea-breeze, smells of sedgy grass and fields by\r\n      the shore, death-messages given in charge to survivors,\r\n  The hiss of the surgeon\xe2\x80\x99s knife, the gnawing teeth of his saw,\r\n  Wheeze, cluck, swash of falling blood, short wild scream, and long,\r\n      dull, tapering groan,\r\n  These so, these irretrievable.\r\n\r\n       37\r\n  You laggards there on guard! look to your arms!\r\n  In at the conquer\xe2\x80\x99d doors they crowd! I am possess\xe2\x80\x99d!\r\n  Embody all presences outlaw\xe2\x80\x99d or suffering,\r\n  See myself in prison shaped like another man,\r\n  And feel the dull unintermitted pain.\r\n\r\n  For me the keepers of convicts shoulder their carbines and keep watch,\r\n  It is I let out in the morning and barr\xe2\x80\x99d at night.\r\n\r\n  Not a mutineer walks handcuff\xe2\x80\x99d to jail but I am handcuff\xe2\x80\x99d to him\r\n      and walk by his side,\r\n  (I am less the jolly one there, and more the silent one with sweat\r\n      on my twitching lips.)\r\n\r\n  Not a youngster is taken for larceny but I go up too, and am tried\r\n      and sentenced.\r\n\r\n  Not a cholera patient lies at the last gasp but I also lie at the last gasp,\r\n  My face is ash-color\xe2\x80\x99d, my sinews gnarl, away from me people retreat.\r\n\r\n  Askers embody themselves in me and I am embodied in them,\r\n  I project my hat, sit shame-faced, and beg.\r\n\r\n       38\r\n  Enough! enough! enough!\r\n  Somehow I have been stunn\xe2\x80\x99d. Stand back!\r\n  Give me a little time beyond my cuff\xe2\x80\x99d head, slumbers, dreams, gaping,\r\n  I discover myself on the verge of a usual mistake.\r\n\r\n  That I could forget the mockers and insults!\r\n  That I could forget the trickling tears and the blows of the\r\n      bludgeons and hammers!\r\n  That I could look with a separate look on my own crucifixion and\r\n      bloody crowning.\r\n\r\n  I remember now,\r\n  I resume the overstaid fraction,\r\n  The grave of rock multiplies what has been confided to it, or to any graves,\r\n  Corpses rise, gashes heal, fastenings roll from me.\r\n\r\n  I troop forth replenish\xe2\x80\x99d with supreme power, one of an average\r\n      unending procession,\r\n  Inland and sea-coast we go, and pass all boundary lines,\r\n  Our swift ordinances on their way over the whole earth,\r\n  The blossoms we wear in our hats the growth of thousands of years.\r\n\r\n  Eleves, I salute you! come forward!\r\n  Continue your annotations, continue your questionings.\r\n\r\n       39\r\n  The friendly and flowing savage, who is he?\r\n  Is he waiting for civilization, or past it and mastering it?\r\n\r\n  Is he some Southwesterner rais\xe2\x80\x99d out-doors? is he Kanadian?\r\n  Is he from the Mississippi country? Iowa, Oregon, California?\r\n  The mountains? prairie-life, bush-life? or sailor from the sea?\r\n\r\n  Wherever he goes men and women accept and desire him,\r\n  They desire he should like them, touch them, speak to them, stay with them.\r\n\r\n  Behavior lawless as snow-flakes, words simple as grass, uncomb\xe2\x80\x99d\r\n      head, laughter, and naivete,\r\n  Slow-stepping feet, common features, common modes and emanations,\r\n  They descend in new forms from the tips of his fingers,\r\n  They are wafted with the odor of his body or breath, they fly out of\r\n      the glance of his eyes.\r\n\r\n       40\r\n  Flaunt of the sunshine I need not your bask--lie over!\r\n  You light surfaces only, I force surfaces and depths also.\r\n\r\n  Earth! you seem to look for something at my hands,\r\n  Say, old top-knot, what do you want?\r\n\r\n  Man or woman, I might tell how I like you, but cannot,\r\n  And might tell what it is in me and what it is in you, but cannot,\r\n  And might tell that pining I have, that pulse of my nights and days.\r\n\r\n  Behold, I do not give lectures or a little charity,\r\n  When I give I give myself.\r\n\r\n  You there, impotent, loose in the knees,\r\n  Open your scarf\xe2\x80\x99d chops till I blow grit within you,\r\n  Spread your palms and lift the flaps of your pockets,\r\n  I am not to be denied, I compel, I have stores plenty and to spare,\r\n  And any thing I have I bestow.\r\n\r\n  I do not ask who you are, that is not important to me,\r\n  You can do nothing and be nothing but what I will infold you.\r\n\r\n  To cotton-field drudge or cleaner of privies I lean,\r\n  On his right cheek I put the family kiss,\r\n  And in my soul I swear I never will deny him.\r\n\r\n  On women fit for conception I start bigger and nimbler babes.\r\n  (This day I am jetting the stuff of far more arrogant republics.)\r\n\r\n  To any one dying, thither I speed and twist the knob of the door.\r\n  Turn the bed-clothes toward the foot of the bed,\r\n  Let the physician and the priest go home.\r\n\r\n  I seize the descending man and raise him with resistless will,\r\n  O despairer, here is my neck,\r\n  By God, you shall not go down! hang your whole weight upon me.\r\n\r\n  I dilate you with tremendous breath, I buoy you up,\r\n  Every room of the house do I fill with an arm\xe2\x80\x99d force,\r\n  Lovers of me, bafflers of graves.\r\n\r\n  Sleep--I and they keep guard all night,\r\n  Not doubt, not decease shall dare to lay finger upon you,\r\n  I have embraced you, and henceforth possess you to myself,\r\n  And when you rise in the morning you will find what I tell you is so.\r\n\r\n       41\r\n  I am he bringing help for the sick as they pant on their backs,\r\n  And for strong upright men I bring yet more needed help.\r\n\r\n  I heard what was said of the universe,\r\n  Heard it and heard it of several thousand years;\r\n  It is middling well as far as it goes--but is that all?\r\n\r\n  Magnifying and applying come I,\r\n  Outbidding at the start the old cautious hucksters,\r\n  Taking myself the exact dimensions of Jehovah,\r\n  Lithographing Kronos, Zeus his son, and Hercules his grandson,\r\n  Buying drafts of Osiris, Isis, Belus, Brahma, Buddha,\r\n  In my portfolio placing Manito loose, Allah on a leaf, the crucifix\r\n      engraved,\r\n  With Odin and the hideous-faced Mexitli and every idol and image,\r\n  Taking them all for what they are worth and not a cent more,\r\n  Admitting they were alive and did the work of their days,\r\n  (They bore mites as for unfledg\xe2\x80\x99d birds who have now to rise and fly\r\n      and sing for themselves,)\r\n  Accepting the rough deific sketches to fill out better in myself,\r\n      bestowing them freely on each man and woman I see,\r\n  Discovering as much or more in a framer framing a house,\r\n  Putting higher claims for him there with his roll\xe2\x80\x99d-up sleeves\r\n      driving the mallet and chisel,\r\n  Not objecting to special revelations, considering a curl of smoke or\r\n      a hair on the back of my hand just as curious as any revelation,\r\n  Lads ahold of fire-engines and hook-and-ladder ropes no less to me\r\n      than the gods of the antique wars,\r\n  Minding their voices peal through the crash of destruction,\r\n  Their brawny limbs passing safe over charr\xe2\x80\x99d laths, their white\r\n      foreheads whole and unhurt out of the flames;\r\n  By the mechanic\xe2\x80\x99s wife with her babe at her nipple interceding for\r\n      every person born,\r\n  Three scythes at harvest whizzing in a row from three lusty angels\r\n      with shirts bagg\xe2\x80\x99d out at their waists,\r\n  The snag-tooth\xe2\x80\x99d hostler with red hair redeeming sins past and to come,\r\n  Selling all he possesses, traveling on foot to fee lawyers for his\r\n      brother and sit by him while he is tried for forgery;\r\n  What was strewn in the amplest strewing the square rod about me, and\r\n      not filling the square rod then,\r\n  The bull and the bug never worshipp\xe2\x80\x99d half enough,\r\n  Dung and dirt more admirable than was dream\xe2\x80\x99d,\r\n  The supernatural of no account, myself waiting my time to be one of\r\n      the supremes,\r\n  The day getting ready for me when I shall do as much good as the\r\n      best, and be as prodigious;\r\n  By my life-lumps! becoming already a creator,\r\n  Putting myself here and now to the ambush\xe2\x80\x99d womb of the shadows.\r\n\r\n\r\n      42\r\n  A call in the midst of the crowd,\r\n  My own voice, orotund sweeping and final.\r\n\r\n  Come my children,\r\n  Come my boys and girls, my women, household and intimates,\r\n  Now the performer launches his nerve, he has pass\xe2\x80\x99d his prelude on\r\n      the reeds within.\r\n\r\n  Easily written loose-finger\xe2\x80\x99d chords--I feel the thrum of your\r\n      climax and close.\r\n\r\n  My head slues round on my neck,\r\n  Music rolls, but not from the organ,\r\n  Folks are around me, but they are no household of mine.\r\n\r\n  Ever the hard unsunk ground,\r\n  Ever the eaters and drinkers, ever the upward and downward sun, ever\r\n      the air and the ceaseless tides,\r\n  Ever myself and my neighbors, refreshing, wicked, real,\r\n  Ever the old inexplicable query, ever that thorn\xe2\x80\x99d thumb, that\r\n      breath of itches and thirsts,\r\n  Ever the vexer\xe2\x80\x99s hoot! hoot! till we find where the sly one hides\r\n      and bring him forth,\r\n  Ever love, ever the sobbing liquid of life,\r\n  Ever the bandage under the chin, ever the trestles of death.\r\n\r\n  Here and there with dimes on the eyes walking,\r\n  To feed the greed of the belly the brains liberally spooning,\r\n  Tickets buying, taking, selling, but in to the feast never once going,\r\n  Many sweating, ploughing, thrashing, and then the chaff for payment\r\n      receiving,\r\n  A few idly owning, and they the wheat continually claiming.\r\n\r\n  This is the city and I am one of the citizens,\r\n  Whatever interests the rest interests me, politics, wars, markets,\r\n      newspapers, schools,\r\n  The mayor and councils, banks, tariffs, steamships, factories,\r\n      stocks, stores, real estate and personal estate.\r\n\r\n  The little plentiful manikins skipping around in collars and tail\xe2\x80\x99d coats\r\n  I am aware who they are, (they are positively not worms or fleas,)\r\n  I acknowledge the duplicates of myself, the weakest and shallowest\r\n      is deathless with me,\r\n  What I do and say the same waits for them,\r\n  Every thought that flounders in me the same flounders in them.\r\n\r\n  I know perfectly well my own egotism,\r\n  Know my omnivorous lines and must not write any less,\r\n  And would fetch you whoever you are flush with myself.\r\n\r\n  Not words of routine this song of mine,\r\n  But abruptly to question, to leap beyond yet nearer bring;\r\n  This printed and bound book--but the printer and the\r\n      printing-office boy?\r\n  The well-taken photographs--but your wife or friend close and solid\r\n      in your arms?\r\n  The black ship mail\xe2\x80\x99d with iron, her mighty guns in her turrets--but\r\n      the pluck of the captain and engineers?\r\n  In the houses the dishes and fare and furniture--but the host and\r\n      hostess, and the look out of their eyes?\r\n  The sky up there--yet here or next door, or across the way?\r\n  The saints and sages in history--but you yourself?\r\n  Sermons, creeds, theology--but the fathomless human brain,\r\n  And what is reason? and what is love? and what is life?\r\n\r\n       43\r\n  I do not despise you priests, all time, the world over,\r\n  My faith is the greatest of faiths and the least of faiths,\r\n  Enclosing worship ancient and modern and all between ancient and modern,\r\n  Believing I shall come again upon the earth after five thousand years,\r\n  Waiting responses from oracles, honoring the gods, saluting the sun,\r\n  Making a fetich of the first rock or stump, powowing with sticks in\r\n      the circle of obis,\r\n  Helping the llama or brahmin as he trims the lamps of the idols,\r\n  Dancing yet through the streets in a phallic procession, rapt and\r\n      austere in the woods a gymnosophist,\r\n  Drinking mead from the skull-cap, to Shastas and Vedas admirant,\r\n      minding the Koran,\r\n  Walking the teokallis, spotted with gore from the stone and knife,\r\n      beating the serpent-skin drum,\r\n  Accepting the Gospels, accepting him that was crucified, knowing\r\n      assuredly that he is divine,\r\n  To the mass kneeling or the puritan\xe2\x80\x99s prayer rising, or sitting\r\n      patiently in a pew,\r\n  Ranting and frothing in my insane crisis, or waiting dead-like till\r\n      my spirit arouses me,\r\n  Looking forth on pavement and land, or outside of pavement and land,\r\n  Belonging to the winders of the circuit of circuits.\r\n\r\n  One of that centripetal and centrifugal gang I turn and talk like\r\n      man leaving charges before a journey.\r\n\r\n  Down-hearted doubters dull and excluded,\r\n  Frivolous, sullen, moping, angry, affected, dishearten\xe2\x80\x99d, atheistical,\r\n  I know every one of you, I know the sea of torment, doubt, despair\r\n      and unbelief.\r\n\r\n  How the flukes splash!\r\n  How they contort rapid as lightning, with spasms and spouts of blood!\r\n\r\n  Be at peace bloody flukes of doubters and sullen mopers,\r\n  I take my place among you as much as among any,\r\n  The past is the push of you, me, all, precisely the same,\r\n  And what is yet untried and afterward is for you, me, all, precisely\r\n      the same.\r\n\r\n  I do not know what is untried and afterward,\r\n  But I know it will in its turn prove sufficient, and cannot fail.\r\n\r\n  Each who passes is consider\xe2\x80\x99d, each who stops is consider\xe2\x80\x99d, not\r\n      single one can it fall.\r\n\r\n  It cannot fall the young man who died and was buried,\r\n  Nor the young woman who died and was put by his side,\r\n  Nor the little child that peep\xe2\x80\x99d in at the door, and then drew back\r\n      and was never seen again,\r\n  Nor the old man who has lived without purpose, and feels it with\r\n      bitterness worse than gall,\r\n  Nor him in the poor house tubercled by rum and the bad disorder,\r\n  Nor the numberless slaughter\xe2\x80\x99d and wreck\xe2\x80\x99d, nor the brutish koboo\r\n      call\xe2\x80\x99d the ordure of humanity,\r\n  Nor the sacs merely floating with open mouths for food to slip in,\r\n  Nor any thing in the earth, or down in the oldest graves of the earth,\r\n  Nor any thing in the myriads of spheres, nor the myriads of myriads\r\n      that inhabit them,\r\n  Nor the present, nor the least wisp that is known.\r\n\r\n       44\r\n  It is time to explain myself--let us stand up.\r\n\r\n  What is known I strip away,\r\n  I launch all men and women forward with me into the Unknown.\r\n\r\n  The clock indicates the moment--but what does eternity indicate?\r\n\r\n  We have thus far exhausted trillions of winters and summers,\r\n  There are trillions ahead, and trillions ahead of them.\r\n\r\n  Births have brought us richness and variety,\r\n  And other births will bring us richness and variety.\r\n\r\n  I do not call one greater and one smaller,\r\n  That which fills its period and place is equal to any.\r\n\r\n  Were mankind murderous or jealous upon you, my brother, my sister?\r\n  I am sorry for you, they are not murderous or jealous upon me,\r\n  All has been gentle with me, I keep no account with lamentation,\r\n  (What have I to do with lamentation?)\r\n\r\n  I am an acme of things accomplish\xe2\x80\x99d, and I an encloser of things to be.\r\n\r\n  My feet strike an apex of the apices of the stairs,\r\n  On every step bunches of ages, and larger bunches between the steps,\r\n  All below duly travel\xe2\x80\x99d, and still I mount and mount.\r\n\r\n  Rise after rise bow the phantoms behind me,\r\n  Afar down I see the huge first Nothing, I know I was even there,\r\n  I waited unseen and always, and slept through the lethargic mist,\r\n  And took my time, and took no hurt from the fetid carbon.\r\n\r\n  Long I was hugg\xe2\x80\x99d close--long and long.\r\n\r\n  Immense have been the preparations for me,\r\n  Faithful and friendly the arms that have help\xe2\x80\x99d me.\r\n\r\n  Cycles ferried my cradle, rowing and rowing like cheerful boatmen,\r\n  For room to me stars kept aside in their own rings,\r\n  They sent influences to look after what was to hold me.\r\n\r\n  Before I was born out of my mother generations guided me,\r\n  My embryo has never been torpid, nothing could overlay it.\r\n\r\n  For it the nebula cohered to an orb,\r\n  The long slow strata piled to rest it on,\r\n  Vast vegetables gave it sustenance,\r\n  Monstrous sauroids transported it in their mouths and deposited it\r\n      with care.\r\n\r\n  All forces have been steadily employ\xe2\x80\x99d to complete and delight me,\r\n  Now on this spot I stand with my robust soul.\r\n\r\n\r\n      45\r\n  O span of youth! ever-push\xe2\x80\x99d elasticity!\r\n  O manhood, balanced, florid and full.\r\n\r\n  My lovers suffocate me,\r\n  Crowding my lips, thick in the pores of my skin,\r\n  Jostling me through streets and public halls, coming naked to me at night,\r\n  Crying by day, Ahoy! from the rocks of the river, swinging and\r\n      chirping over my head,\r\n  Calling my name from flower-beds, vines, tangled underbrush,\r\n  Lighting on every moment of my life,\r\n  Bussing my body with soft balsamic busses,\r\n  Noiselessly passing handfuls out of their hearts and giving them to be mine.\r\n\r\n  Old age superbly rising! O welcome, ineffable grace of dying days!\r\n\r\n  Every condition promulges not only itself, it promulges what grows\r\n      after and out of itself,\r\n  And the dark hush promulges as much as any.\r\n\r\n  I open my scuttle at night and see the far-sprinkled systems,\r\n  And all I see multiplied as high as I can cipher edge but the rim of\r\n      the farther systems.\r\n\r\n  Wider and wider they spread, expanding, always expanding,\r\n  Outward and outward and forever outward.\r\n\r\n  My sun has his sun and round him obediently wheels,\r\n  He joins with his partners a group of superior circuit,\r\n  And greater sets follow, making specks of the greatest inside them.\r\n\r\n  There is no stoppage and never can be stoppage,\r\n  If I, you, and the worlds, and all beneath or upon their surfaces,\r\n      were this moment reduced back to a pallid float, it would\r\n      not avail the long run,\r\n  We should surely bring up again where we now stand,\r\n  And surely go as much farther, and then farther and farther.\r\n\r\n  A few quadrillions of eras, a few octillions of cubic leagues, do\r\n      not hazard the span or make it impatient,\r\n  They are but parts, any thing is but a part.\r\n\r\n  See ever so far, there is limitless space outside of that,\r\n  Count ever so much, there is limitless time around that.\r\n\r\n  My rendezvous is appointed, it is certain,\r\n  The Lord will be there and wait till I come on perfect terms,\r\n  The great Camerado, the lover true for whom I pine will be there.\r\n\r\n       46\r\n  I know I have the best of time and space, and was never measured and\r\n      never will be measured.\r\n\r\n  I tramp a perpetual journey, (come listen all!)\r\n  My signs are a rain-proof coat, good shoes, and a staff cut from the woods,\r\n  No friend of mine takes his ease in my chair,\r\n  I have no chair, no church, no philosophy,\r\n  I lead no man to a dinner-table, library, exchange,\r\n  But each man and each woman of you I lead upon a knoll,\r\n  My left hand hooking you round the waist,\r\n  My right hand pointing to landscapes of continents and the public road.\r\n\r\n  Not I, not any one else can travel that road for you,\r\n  You must travel it for yourself.\r\n\r\n  It is not far, it is within reach,\r\n  Perhaps you have been on it since you were born and did not know,\r\n  Perhaps it is everywhere on water and on land.\r\n\r\n  Shoulder your duds dear son, and I will mine, and let us hasten forth,\r\n  Wonderful cities and free nations we shall fetch as we go.\r\n\r\n  If you tire, give me both burdens, and rest the chuff of your hand\r\n      on my hip,\r\n  And in due time you shall repay the same service to me,\r\n  For after we start we never lie by again.\r\n\r\n  This day before dawn I ascended a hill and look\xe2\x80\x99d at the crowded heaven,\r\n  And I said to my spirit When we become the enfolders of those orbs,\r\n      and the pleasure and knowledge of every thing in them, shall we\r\n      be fill\xe2\x80\x99d and satisfied then?\r\n  And my spirit said No, we but level that lift to pass and continue beyond.\r\n\r\n  You are also asking me questions and I hear you,\r\n  I answer that I cannot answer, you must find out for yourself.\r\n\r\n  Sit a while dear son,\r\n  Here are biscuits to eat and here is milk to drink,\r\n  But as soon as you sleep and renew yourself in sweet clothes, I kiss you\r\n      with a good-by kiss and open the gate for your egress hence.\r\n\r\n  Long enough have you dream\xe2\x80\x99d contemptible dreams,\r\n  Now I wash the gum from your eyes,\r\n  You must habit yourself to the dazzle of the light and of every\r\n      moment of your life.\r\n\r\n  Long have you timidly waded holding a plank by the shore,\r\n  Now I will you to be a bold swimmer,\r\n  To jump off in the midst of the sea, rise again, nod to me, shout,\r\n      and laughingly dash with your hair.\r\n\r\n       47\r\n  I am the teacher of athletes,\r\n  He that by me spreads a wider breast than my own proves the width of my own,\r\n  He most honors my style who learns under it to destroy the teacher.\r\n\r\n  The boy I love, the same becomes a man not through derived power,\r\n      but in his own right,\r\n  Wicked rather than virtuous out of conformity or fear,\r\n  Fond of his sweetheart, relishing well his steak,\r\n  Unrequited love or a slight cutting him worse than sharp steel cuts,\r\n  First-rate to ride, to fight, to hit the bull\xe2\x80\x99s eye, to sail a\r\n      skiff, to sing a song or play on the banjo,\r\n  Preferring scars and the beard and faces pitted with small-pox over\r\n      all latherers,\r\n  And those well-tann\xe2\x80\x99d to those that keep out of the sun.\r\n\r\n  I teach straying from me, yet who can stray from me?\r\n  I follow you whoever you are from the present hour,\r\n  My words itch at your ears till you understand them.\r\n\r\n  I do not say these things for a dollar or to fill up the time while\r\n      I wait for a boat,\r\n  (It is you talking just as much as myself, I act as the tongue of you,\r\n  Tied in your mouth, in mine it begins to be loosen\xe2\x80\x99d.)\r\n\r\n  I swear I will never again mention love or death inside a house,\r\n  And I swear I will never translate myself at all, only to him or her\r\n      who privately stays with me in the open air.\r\n\r\n  If you would understand me go to the heights or water-shore,\r\n  The nearest gnat is an explanation, and a drop or motion of waves key,\r\n  The maul, the oar, the hand-saw, second my words.\r\n\r\n  No shutter\xe2\x80\x99d room or school can commune with me,\r\n  But roughs and little children better than they.\r\n\r\n  The young mechanic is closest to me, he knows me well,\r\n  The woodman that takes his axe and jug with him shall take me with\r\n      him all day,\r\n  The farm-boy ploughing in the field feels good at the sound of my voice,\r\n  In vessels that sail my words sail, I go with fishermen and seamen\r\n      and love them.\r\n\r\n  The soldier camp\xe2\x80\x99d or upon the march is mine,\r\n  On the night ere the pending battle many seek me, and I do not fail them,\r\n  On that solemn night (it may be their last) those that know me seek me.\r\n  My face rubs to the hunter\xe2\x80\x99s face when he lies down alone in his blanket,\r\n  The driver thinking of me does not mind the jolt of his wagon,\r\n  The young mother and old mother comprehend me,\r\n  The girl and the wife rest the needle a moment and forget where they are,\r\n  They and all would resume what I have told them.\r\n\r\n       48\r\n  I have said that the soul is not more than the body,\r\n  And I have said that the body is not more than the soul,\r\n  And nothing, not God, is greater to one than one\xe2\x80\x99s self is,\r\n  And whoever walks a furlong without sympathy walks to his own\r\n      funeral drest in his shroud,\r\n  And I or you pocketless of a dime may purchase the pick of the earth,\r\n  And to glance with an eye or show a bean in its pod confounds the\r\n      learning of all times,\r\n  And there is no trade or employment but the young man following it\r\n      may become a hero,\r\n  And there is no object so soft but it makes a hub for the wheel\xe2\x80\x99d universe,\r\n  And I say to any man or woman, Let your soul stand cool and composed\r\n      before a million universes.\r\n\r\n  And I say to mankind, Be not curious about God,\r\n  For I who am curious about each am not curious about God,\r\n  (No array of terms can say how much I am at peace about God and\r\n      about death.)\r\n\r\n  I hear and behold God in every object, yet understand God not in the least,\r\n  Nor do I understand who there can be more wonderful than myself.\r\n\r\n  Why should I wish to see God better than this day?\r\n  I see something of God each hour of the twenty-four, and each moment then,\r\n  In the faces of men and women I see God, and in my own face in the glass,\r\n  I find letters from God dropt in the street, and every one is sign\xe2\x80\x99d\r\n      by God\xe2\x80\x99s name,\r\n  And I leave them where they are, for I know that wheresoe\xe2\x80\x99er I go,\r\n  Others will punctually come for ever and ever.\r\n\r\n       49\r\n  And as to you Death, and you bitter hug of mortality, it is idle to\r\n      try to alarm me.\r\n\r\n  To his work without flinching the accoucheur comes,\r\n  I see the elder-hand pressing receiving supporting,\r\n  I recline by the sills of the exquisite flexible doors,\r\n  And mark the outlet, and mark the relief and escape.\r\n\r\n  And as to you Corpse I think you are good manure, but that does not\r\n      offend me,\r\n  I smell the white roses sweet-scented and growing,\r\n  I reach to the leafy lips, I reach to the polish\xe2\x80\x99d breasts of melons.\r\n\r\n  And as to you Life I reckon you are the leavings of many deaths,\r\n  (No doubt I have died myself ten thousand times before.)\r\n\r\n  I hear you whispering there O stars of heaven,\r\n  O suns--O grass of graves--O perpetual transfers and promotions,\r\n  If you do not say any thing how can I say any thing?\r\n\r\n  Of the turbid pool that lies in the autumn forest,\r\n  Of the moon that descends the steeps of the soughing twilight,\r\n  Toss, sparkles of day and dusk--toss on the black stems that decay\r\n      in the muck,\r\n  Toss to the moaning gibberish of the dry limbs.\r\n\r\n  I ascend from the moon, I ascend from the night,\r\n  I perceive that the ghastly glimmer is noonday sunbeams reflected,\r\n  And debouch to the steady and central from the offspring great or small.\r\n\r\n       50\r\n  There is that in me--I do not know what it is--but I know it is in me.\r\n\r\n  Wrench\xe2\x80\x99d and sweaty--calm and cool then my body becomes,\r\n  I sleep--I sleep long.\r\n\r\n  I do not know it--it is without name--it is a word unsaid,\r\n  It is not in any dictionary, utterance, symbol.\r\n\r\n  Something it swings on more than the earth I swing on,\r\n  To it the creation is the friend whose embracing awakes me.\r\n\r\n  Perhaps I might tell more. Outlines! I plead for my brothers and sisters.\r\n\r\n  Do you see O my brothers and sisters?\r\n  It is not chaos or death--it is form, union, plan--it is eternal\r\n      life--it is Happiness.\r\n\r\n       51\r\n  The past and present wilt--I have fill\xe2\x80\x99d them, emptied them.\r\n  And proceed to fill my next fold of the future.\r\n\r\n  Listener up there! what have you to confide to me?\r\n  Look in my face while I snuff the sidle of evening,\r\n  (Talk honestly, no one else hears you, and I stay only a minute longer.)\r\n\r\n  Do I contradict myself?\r\n  Very well then I contradict myself,\r\n  (I am large, I contain multitudes.)\r\n\r\n  I concentrate toward them that are nigh, I wait on the door-slab.\r\n\r\n  Who has done his day\xe2\x80\x99s work? who will soonest be through with his supper?\r\n  Who wishes to walk with me?\r\n\r\n  Will you speak before I am gone? will you prove already too late?\r\n\r\n       52\r\n  The spotted hawk swoops by and accuses me, he complains of my gab\r\n      and my loitering.\r\n\r\n  I too am not a bit tamed, I too am untranslatable,\r\n  I sound my barbaric yawp over the roofs of the world.\r\n\r\n  The last scud of day holds back for me,\r\n  It flings my likeness after the rest and true as any on the shadow\xe2\x80\x99d wilds,\r\n  It coaxes me to the vapor and the dusk.\r\n\r\n  I depart as air, I shake my white locks at the runaway sun,\r\n  I effuse my flesh in eddies, and drift it in lacy jags.\r\n\r\n  I bequeath myself to the dirt to grow from the grass I love,\r\n  If you want me again look for me under your boot-soles.\r\n\r\n  You will hardly know who I am or what I mean,\r\n  But I shall be good health to you nevertheless,\r\n  And filter and fibre your blood.\r\n\r\n  Failing to fetch me at first keep encouraged,\r\n  Missing me one place search another,\r\n  I stop somewhere waiting for you.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nBOOK IV.  CHILDREN OF ADAM\r\n\r\n\r\nTo the Garden the World\r\n\r\n  To the garden the world anew ascending,\r\n  Potent mates, daughters, sons, preluding,\r\n  The love, the life of their bodies, meaning and being,\r\n  Curious here behold my resurrection after slumber,\r\n  The revolving cycles in their wide sweep having brought me again,\r\n  Amorous, mature, all beautiful to me, all wondrous,\r\n  My limbs and the quivering fire that ever plays through them, for\r\n      reasons, most wondrous,\r\n  Existing I peer and penetrate still,\r\n  Content with the present, content with the past,\r\n  By my side or back of me Eve following,\r\n  Or in front, and I following her just the same.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nFrom Pent-Up Aching Rivers\r\n\r\n  From pent-up aching rivers,\r\n  From that of myself without which I were nothing,\r\n  From what I am determin\xe2\x80\x99d to make illustrious, even if I stand sole\r\n      among men,\r\n  From my own voice resonant, singing the phallus,\r\n  Singing the song of procreation,\r\n  Singing the need of superb children and therein superb grown people,\r\n  Singing the muscular urge and the blending,\r\n  Singing the bedfellow\xe2\x80\x99s song, (O resistless yearning!\r\n  O for any and each the body correlative attracting!\r\n  O for you whoever you are your correlative body! O it, more than all\r\n      else, you delighting!)\r\n  From the hungry gnaw that eats me night and day,\r\n  From native moments, from bashful pains, singing them,\r\n  Seeking something yet unfound though I have diligently sought it\r\n      many a long year,\r\n  Singing the true song of the soul fitful at random,\r\n  Renascent with grossest Nature or among animals,\r\n  Of that, of them and what goes with them my poems informing,\r\n  Of the smell of apples and lemons, of the pairing of birds,\r\n  Of the wet of woods, of the lapping of waves,\r\n  Of the mad pushes of waves upon the land, I them chanting,\r\n  The overture lightly sounding, the strain anticipating,\r\n  The welcome nearness, the sight of the perfect body,\r\n  The swimmer swimming naked in the bath, or motionless on his back\r\n      lying and floating,\r\n  The female form approaching, I pensive, love-flesh tremulous aching,\r\n  The divine list for myself or you or for any one making,\r\n  The face, the limbs, the index from head to foot, and what it arouses,\r\n  The mystic deliria, the madness amorous, the utter abandonment,\r\n  (Hark close and still what I now whisper to you,\r\n  I love you, O you entirely possess me,\r\n  O that you and I escape from the rest and go utterly off, free and lawless,\r\n  Two hawks in the air, two fishes swimming in the sea not more\r\n      lawless than we;)\r\n  The furious storm through me careering, I passionately trembling.\r\n  The oath of the inseparableness of two together, of the woman that\r\n      loves me and whom I love more than my life, that oath swearing,\r\n  (O I willingly stake all for you,\r\n  O let me be lost if it must be so!\r\n  O you and I! what is it to us what the rest do or think?\r\n  What is all else to us? only that we enjoy each other and exhaust\r\n      each other if it must be so;)\r\n  From the master, the pilot I yield the vessel to,\r\n  The general commanding me, commanding all, from him permission taking,\r\n  From time the programme hastening, (I have loiter\xe2\x80\x99d too long as it is,)\r\n  From sex, from the warp and from the woof,\r\n  From privacy, from frequent repinings alone,\r\n  From plenty of persons near and yet the right person not near,\r\n  From the soft sliding of hands over me and thrusting of fingers\r\n      through my hair and beard,\r\n  From the long sustain\xe2\x80\x99d kiss upon the mouth or bosom,\r\n  From the close pressure that makes me or any man drunk, fainting\r\n      with excess,\r\n  From what the divine husband knows, from the work of fatherhood,\r\n  From exultation, victory and relief, from the bedfellow\xe2\x80\x99s embrace in\r\n      the night,\r\n  From the act-poems of eyes, hands, hips and bosoms,\r\n  From the cling of the trembling arm,\r\n  From the bending curve and the clinch,\r\n  From side by side the pliant coverlet off-throwing,\r\n  From the one so unwilling to have me leave, and me just as unwilling\r\n      to leave,\r\n  (Yet a moment O tender waiter, and I return,)\r\n  From the hour of shining stars and dropping dews,\r\n  From the night a moment I emerging flitting out,\r\n  Celebrate you act divine and you children prepared for,\r\n  And you stalwart loins.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nI Sing the Body Electric\r\n\r\n       1\r\n  I sing the body electric,\r\n  The armies of those I love engirth me and I engirth them,\r\n  They will not let me off till I go with them, respond to them,\r\n  And discorrupt them, and charge them full with the charge of the soul.\r\n\r\n  Was it doubted that those who corrupt their own bodies conceal themselves?\r\n  And if those who defile the living are as bad as they who defile the dead?\r\n  And if the body does not do fully as much as the soul?\r\n  And if the body were not the soul, what is the soul?\r\n\r\n       2\r\n  The love of the body of man or woman balks account, the body itself\r\n      balks account,\r\n  That of the male is perfect, and that of the female is perfect.\r\n\r\n  The expression of the face balks account,\r\n  But the expression of a well-made man appears not only in his face,\r\n  It is in his limbs and joints also, it is curiously in the joints of\r\n      his hips and wrists,\r\n  It is in his walk, the carriage of his neck, the flex of his waist\r\n      and knees, dress does not hide him,\r\n  The strong sweet quality he has strikes through the cotton and broadcloth,\r\n  To see him pass conveys as much as the best poem, perhaps more,\r\n  You linger to see his back, and the back of his neck and shoulder-side.\r\n\r\n  The sprawl and fulness of babes, the bosoms and heads of women, the\r\n      folds of their dress, their style as we pass in the street, the\r\n      contour of their shape downwards,\r\n  The swimmer naked in the swimming-bath, seen as he swims through\r\n      the transparent green-shine, or lies with his face up and rolls\r\n      silently to and from the heave of the water,\r\n  The bending forward and backward of rowers in row-boats, the\r\n      horse-man in his saddle,\r\n  Girls, mothers, house-keepers, in all their performances,\r\n  The group of laborers seated at noon-time with their open\r\n      dinner-kettles, and their wives waiting,\r\n  The female soothing a child, the farmer\xe2\x80\x99s daughter in the garden or\r\n      cow-yard,\r\n  The young fellow hosing corn, the sleigh-driver driving his six\r\n      horses through the crowd,\r\n  The wrestle of wrestlers, two apprentice-boys, quite grown, lusty,\r\n      good-natured, native-born, out on the vacant lot at sundown after work,\r\n  The coats and caps thrown down, the embrace of love and resistance,\r\n  The upper-hold and under-hold, the hair rumpled over and blinding the eyes;\r\n  The march of firemen in their own costumes, the play of masculine\r\n      muscle through clean-setting trowsers and waist-straps,\r\n  The slow return from the fire, the pause when the bell strikes\r\n      suddenly again, and the listening on the alert,\r\n  The natural, perfect, varied attitudes, the bent head, the curv\xe2\x80\x99d\r\n      neck and the counting;\r\n  Such-like I love--I loosen myself, pass freely, am at the mother\xe2\x80\x99s\r\n      breast with the little child,\r\n  Swim with the swimmers, wrestle with wrestlers, march in line with\r\n      the firemen, and pause, listen, count.\r\n\r\n       3\r\n  I knew a man, a common farmer, the father of five sons,\r\n  And in them the fathers of sons, and in them the fathers of sons.\r\n\r\n  This man was a wonderful vigor, calmness, beauty of person,\r\n  The shape of his head, the pale yellow and white of his hair and\r\n      beard, the immeasurable meaning of his black eyes, the richness\r\n      and breadth of his manners,\r\n  These I used to go and visit him to see, he was wise also,\r\n  He was six feet tall, he was over eighty years old, his sons were\r\n      massive, clean, bearded, tan-faced, handsome,\r\n  They and his daughters loved him, all who saw him loved him,\r\n  They did not love him by allowance, they loved him with personal love,\r\n  He drank water only, the blood show\xe2\x80\x99d like scarlet through the\r\n      clear-brown skin of his face,\r\n  He was a frequent gunner and fisher, he sail\xe2\x80\x99d his boat himself, he\r\n      had a fine one presented to him by a ship-joiner, he had\r\n      fowling-pieces presented to him by men that loved him,\r\n  When he went with his five sons and many grand-sons to hunt or fish,\r\n      you would pick him out as the most beautiful and vigorous of the gang,\r\n  You would wish long and long to be with him, you would wish to sit\r\n      by him in the boat that you and he might touch each other.\r\n\r\n       4\r\n  I have perceiv\xe2\x80\x99d that to be with those I like is enough,\r\n  To stop in company with the rest at evening is enough,\r\n  To be surrounded by beautiful, curious, breathing, laughing flesh is enough,\r\n  To pass among them or touch any one, or rest my arm ever so lightly\r\n      round his or her neck for a moment, what is this then?\r\n  I do not ask any more delight, I swim in it as in a sea.\r\n\r\n  There is something in staying close to men and women and looking\r\n      on them, and in the contact and odor of them, that pleases the soul well,\r\n  All things please the soul, but these please the soul well.\r\n\r\n       5\r\n  This is the female form,\r\n  A divine nimbus exhales from it from head to foot,\r\n  It attracts with fierce undeniable attraction,\r\n  I am drawn by its breath as if I were no more than a helpless vapor,\r\n      all falls aside but myself and it,\r\n  Books, art, religion, time, the visible and solid earth, and what\r\n      was expected of heaven or fear\xe2\x80\x99d of hell, are now consumed,\r\n  Mad filaments, ungovernable shoots play out of it, the response\r\n      likewise ungovernable,\r\n  Hair, bosom, hips, bend of legs, negligent falling hands all\r\n      diffused, mine too diffused,\r\n  Ebb stung by the flow and flow stung by the ebb, love-flesh swelling\r\n      and deliciously aching,\r\n  Limitless limpid jets of love hot and enormous, quivering jelly of\r\n      love, white-blow and delirious nice,\r\n  Bridegroom night of love working surely and softly into the prostrate dawn,\r\n  Undulating into the willing and yielding day,\r\n  Lost in the cleave of the clasping and sweet-flesh\xe2\x80\x99d day.\r\n\r\n  This the nucleus--after the child is born of woman, man is born of woman,\r\n  This the bath of birth, this the merge of small and large, and the\r\n      outlet again.\r\n\r\n  Be not ashamed women, your privilege encloses the rest, and is the\r\n      exit of the rest,\r\n  You are the gates of the body, and you are the gates of the soul.\r\n\r\n  The female contains all qualities and tempers them,\r\n  She is in her place and moves with perfect balance,\r\n  She is all things duly veil\xe2\x80\x99d, she is both passive and active,\r\n  She is to conceive daughters as well as sons, and sons as well as daughters.\r\n\r\n  As I see my soul reflected in Nature,\r\n  As I see through a mist, One with inexpressible completeness,\r\n      sanity, beauty,\r\n  See the bent head and arms folded over the breast, the Female I see.\r\n\r\n       6\r\n  The male is not less the soul nor more, he too is in his place,\r\n  He too is all qualities, he is action and power,\r\n  The flush of the known universe is in him,\r\n  Scorn becomes him well, and appetite and defiance become him well,\r\n  The wildest largest passions, bliss that is utmost, sorrow that is\r\n      utmost become him well, pride is for him,\r\n  The full-spread pride of man is calming and excellent to the soul,\r\n  Knowledge becomes him, he likes it always, he brings every thing to\r\n      the test of himself,\r\n  Whatever the survey, whatever the sea and the sail he strikes\r\n      soundings at last only here,\r\n  (Where else does he strike soundings except here?)\r\n\r\n  The man\xe2\x80\x99s body is sacred and the woman\xe2\x80\x99s body is sacred,\r\n  No matter who it is, it is sacred--is it the meanest one in the\r\n      laborers\xe2\x80\x99 gang?\r\n  Is it one of the dull-faced immigrants just landed on the wharf?\r\n  Each belongs here or anywhere just as much as the well-off, just as\r\n      much as you,\r\n  Each has his or her place in the procession.\r\n\r\n  (All is a procession,\r\n  The universe is a procession with measured and perfect motion.)\r\n\r\n  Do you know so much yourself that you call the meanest ignorant?\r\n  Do you suppose you have a right to a good sight, and he or she has\r\n      no right to a sight?\r\n  Do you think matter has cohered together from its diffuse float, and\r\n      the soil is on the surface, and water runs and vegetation sprouts,\r\n  For you only, and not for him and her?\r\n\r\n       7\r\n  A man\xe2\x80\x99s body at auction,\r\n  (For before the war I often go to the slave-mart and watch the sale,)\r\n  I help the auctioneer, the sloven does not half know his business.\r\n\r\n  Gentlemen look on this wonder,\r\n  Whatever the bids of the bidders they cannot be high enough for it,\r\n  For it the globe lay preparing quintillions of years without one\r\n      animal or plant,\r\n  For it the revolving cycles truly and steadily roll\xe2\x80\x99d.\r\n\r\n  In this head the all-baffling brain,\r\n  In it and below it the makings of heroes.\r\n\r\n  Examine these limbs, red, black, or white, they are cunning in\r\n      tendon and nerve,\r\n  They shall be stript that you may see them.\r\n\r\n  Exquisite senses, life-lit eyes, pluck, volition,\r\n  Flakes of breast-muscle, pliant backbone and neck, flesh not flabby,\r\n      good-sized arms and legs,\r\n  And wonders within there yet.\r\n\r\n  Within there runs blood,\r\n  The same old blood! the same red-running blood!\r\n  There swells and jets a heart, there all passions, desires,\r\n      reachings, aspirations,\r\n  (Do you think they are not there because they are not express\xe2\x80\x99d in\r\n      parlors and lecture-rooms?)\r\n\r\n  This is not only one man, this the father of those who shall be\r\n      fathers in their turns,\r\n  In him the start of populous states and rich republics,\r\n  Of him countless immortal lives with countless embodiments and enjoyments.\r\n\r\n  How do you know who shall come from the offspring of his offspring\r\n      through the centuries?\r\n  (Who might you find you have come from yourself, if you could trace\r\n      back through the centuries?)\r\n\r\n       8\r\n  A woman\xe2\x80\x99s body at auction,\r\n  She too is not only herself, she is the teeming mother of mothers,\r\n  She is the bearer of them that shall grow and be mates to the mothers.\r\n\r\n  Have you ever loved the body of a woman?\r\n  Have you ever loved the body of a man?\r\n  Do you not see that these are exactly the same to all in all nations\r\n      and times all over the earth?\r\n\r\n  If any thing is sacred the human body is sacred,\r\n  And the glory and sweet of a man is the token of manhood untainted,\r\n  And in man or woman a clean, strong, firm-fibred body, is more\r\n      beautiful than the most beautiful face.\r\n\r\n  Have you seen the fool that corrupted his own live body? or the fool\r\n      that corrupted her own live body?\r\n  For they do not conceal themselves, and cannot conceal themselves.\r\n\r\n       9\r\n  O my body! I dare not desert the likes of you in other men and\r\n      women, nor the likes of the parts of you,\r\n  I believe the likes of you are to stand or fall with the likes of\r\n      the soul, (and that they are the soul,)\r\n  I believe the likes of you shall stand or fall with my poems, and\r\n      that they are my poems,\r\n  Man\xe2\x80\x99s, woman\xe2\x80\x99s, child, youth\xe2\x80\x99s, wife\xe2\x80\x99s, husband\xe2\x80\x99s, mother\xe2\x80\x99s,\r\n      father\xe2\x80\x99s, young man\xe2\x80\x99s, young woman\xe2\x80\x99s poems,\r\n  Head, neck, hair, ears, drop and tympan of the ears,\r\n  Eyes, eye-fringes, iris of the eye, eyebrows, and the waking or\r\n      sleeping of the lids,\r\n  Mouth, tongue, lips, teeth, roof of the mouth, jaws, and the jaw-hinges,\r\n  Nose, nostrils of the nose, and the partition,\r\n  Cheeks, temples, forehead, chin, throat, back of the neck, neck-slue,\r\n  Strong shoulders, manly beard, scapula, hind-shoulders, and the\r\n      ample side-round of the chest,\r\n  Upper-arm, armpit, elbow-socket, lower-arm, arm-sinews, arm-bones,\r\n  Wrist and wrist-joints, hand, palm, knuckles, thumb, forefinger,\r\n      finger-joints, finger-nails,\r\n  Broad breast-front, curling hair of the breast, breast-bone, breast-side,\r\n  Ribs, belly, backbone, joints of the backbone,\r\n  Hips, hip-sockets, hip-strength, inward and outward round,\r\n      man-balls, man-root,\r\n  Strong set of thighs, well carrying the trunk above,\r\n  Leg-fibres, knee, knee-pan, upper-leg, under-leg,\r\n  Ankles, instep, foot-ball, toes, toe-joints, the heel;\r\n  All attitudes, all the shapeliness, all the belongings of my or your\r\n      body or of any one\xe2\x80\x99s body, male or female,\r\n  The lung-sponges, the stomach-sac, the bowels sweet and clean,\r\n  The brain in its folds inside the skull-frame,\r\n  Sympathies, heart-valves, palate-valves, sexuality, maternity,\r\n  Womanhood, and all that is a woman, and the man that comes from woman,\r\n  The womb, the teats, nipples, breast-milk, tears, laughter, weeping,\r\n      love-looks, love-perturbations and risings,\r\n  The voice, articulation, language, whispering, shouting aloud,\r\n  Food, drink, pulse, digestion, sweat, sleep, walking, swimming,\r\n  Poise on the hips, leaping, reclining, embracing, arm-curving and tightening,\r\n  The continual changes of the flex of the mouth, and around the eyes,\r\n  The skin, the sunburnt shade, freckles, hair,\r\n  The curious sympathy one feels when feeling with the hand the naked\r\n      meat of the body,\r\n  The circling rivers the breath, and breathing it in and out,\r\n  The beauty of the waist, and thence of the hips, and thence downward\r\n      toward the knees,\r\n  The thin red jellies within you or within me, the bones and the\r\n      marrow in the bones,\r\n  The exquisite realization of health;\r\n  O I say these are not the parts and poems of the body only, but of the soul,\r\n  O I say now these are the soul!\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nA Woman Waits for Me\r\n\r\n  A woman waits for me, she contains all, nothing is lacking,\r\n  Yet all were lacking if sex were lacking, or if the moisture of the\r\n      right man were lacking.\r\n\r\n  Sex contains all, bodies, souls,\r\n  Meanings, proofs, purities, delicacies, results, promulgations,\r\n  Songs, commands, health, pride, the maternal mystery, the seminal milk,\r\n  All hopes, benefactions, bestowals, all the passions, loves,\r\n      beauties, delights of the earth,\r\n  All the governments, judges, gods, follow\xe2\x80\x99d persons of the earth,\r\n  These are contain\xe2\x80\x99d in sex as parts of itself and justifications of itself.\r\n\r\n  Without shame the man I like knows and avows the deliciousness of his sex,\r\n  Without shame the woman I like knows and avows hers.\r\n\r\n  Now I will dismiss myself from impassive women,\r\n  I will go stay with her who waits for me, and with those women that\r\n      are warm-blooded and sufficient for me,\r\n  I see that they understand me and do not deny me,\r\n  I see that they are worthy of me, I will be the robust husband of\r\n      those women.\r\n\r\n  They are not one jot less than I am,\r\n  They are tann\xe2\x80\x99d in the face by shining suns and blowing winds,\r\n  Their flesh has the old divine suppleness and
